class="css-6n7j50"><button aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="More sharing options" class="css-16ogagc" data-testid=""><svg class="css-uhuo44" height="13" viewbox="0 0 16 13" width="16"><path clip-rule="evenodd" d="M15.406 5.359L8.978 0v3.215C3.82 3.215.406 8.107.406 12.66 1.653 9.133 4.29 7.517 8.978 7.517v3.2l6.428-5.358z" fill="#000" fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></button></div></li><li class="css-60hakz"></li></ul></div></div></li></ul></div></div></header><section class="meteredContent css-1i2y565" itemprop="articleBody" name="articleBody"><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">WASHINGTON — After oil installations were blown up in Saudi Arabia over the weekend, President Trump declared that the United States was <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://twitter.com/realdonaldtrump/status/1173368423381962752" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">“locked and loaded,”</a> a phrase that seemed to suggest he was ready to strike back. But then he promised to wait for Saudi Arabia to tell him “under what terms we would proceed.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">His message on Twitter offered a remarkable insight into the deference Mr. Trump gives to the Saudi royal family and touched off a torrent of criticism from those who have long accused him of doing Riyadh’s bidding while sweeping <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/06/19/world/middleeast/jamal-khashoggi-Mohammed-bin-Salman.html?module=inline" title="">Saudi violations of human rights</a> and international norms under the rug.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">It was hard to imagine him allowing NATO, or a European ally, such latitude to determine how the United States should respond. But for Mr. Trump, the Saudis have always been a special case, their economic import having often overwhelmed other considerations in his mind.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Whether, and how, to commit American forces is one of the most critical decisions any American president can make, but Mr. Trump’s comment gave the impression that he was outsourcing the decision.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The fact that the other country was Saudi Arabia — a difficult ally that came under intense criticism for the <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/11/16/us/politics/cia-saudi-crown-prince-khashoggi.html?action=click&amp;module=inline&amp;pgtype=Article&amp;region=Footer" title="">killing and dismemberment of Jamal Khashoggi</a>, the dissident and Washington Post columnist — reinforced the longstanding criticism that the energy-rich kingdom buys American support.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“What struck me about that tweet was not just that it’s obviously wrong to allow Saudi Arabia to dictate our foreign policy, but that the president doesn’t seem to be aware of how submissive it makes him look to say that,” said Representative Tom Malinowski, Democrat of New Jersey and a former assistant secretary of state.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“It is a big deal to attack oil fields,” Mr. Malinowski added. “It does affect more than just Saudi Arabia’s interests. But whatever we do, we have to do what’s best for us and we have to recognize that the Saudis have a profound bias.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Trump told reporters on Monday that he had not “promised” to protect the Saudis and that he would “sit down with the Saudis and work something out.” But he expressed caution, suggesting that for all of his bellicose language, he was not rushing toward a military conflict.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Asked whether Iran was behind the attack, Mr. Trump said, “It is looking that way.” But he stopped short of definitive confirmation. “That is being checked out right now,” he added.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Trump warned that the United States had fearsome military abilities and was prepared for war if necessary.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-79elbk" data-testid="photoviewer-wrapper"><div class="css-z3e15g" data-testid="photoviewer-wrapper-hidden"></div><div class="css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15" data-testid="photoviewer-children"><figure aria-label="media" class="css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0" itemid="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/16/us/politics/16dc-prexy2/merlin_160902594_d4b298b2-a01e-4e33-88b7-880ddeb56f9d-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp" itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" role="group"><div class="css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Image</span><img alt="A satellite image showing damage to oil and gas infrastructure after an attack in Abqaig, Saudi Arabia." class="css-1m50asq" itemid="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/16/us/politics/16dc-prexy2/merlin_160902594_d4b298b2-a01e-4e33-88b7-880ddeb56f9d-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale" itemprop="url" sizes="((min-width: 600px) and (max-width: 1004px)) 84vw, (min-width: 1005px) 60vw, 100vw" src="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/16/us/politics/16dc-prexy2/merlin_160902594_d4b298b2-a01e-4e33-88b7-880ddeb56f9d-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale" srcset="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/16/us/politics/16dc-prexy2/merlin_160902594_d4b298b2-a01e-4e33-88b7-880ddeb56f9d-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 600w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/16/us/politics/16dc-prexy2/merlin_160902594_d4b298b2-a01e-4e33-88b7-880ddeb56f9d-jumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/16/us/politics/16dc-prexy2/merlin_160902594_d4b298b2-a01e-4e33-88b7-880ddeb56f9d-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1920w"/></div><figcaption class="css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0" itemprop="caption description"><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0">A satellite image showing damage to oil and gas infrastructure after an attack in Abqaig, Saudi Arabia.</span><span class="css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90" itemprop="copyrightHolder"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Credit</span><span>Agence France-Presse — Getty Images</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“But with all that being said, we would certainly like to avoid it,” he added. “I know they would like to make a deal,” he said of the Iranians, whom he has been trying to draw into talks over their nuclear program. “At some point, it will work out.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">There is no evidence it will work out soon. The Iranian Foreign Ministry dismissed the notion on Monday that President Hassan Rouhani would meet Mr. Trump in New York next week when both are scheduled to attend the opening of the United Nations General Assembly. While Mr. Trump said in June that a meeting could happen without preconditions, and his own aides, including Secretary of State Mike Pompeo and Treasury Secretary Steven Mnuchin, repeated it last week, Mr. Trump <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://twitter.com/realDonaldTrump/status/1173371482812162048" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">called that “fake news”</a> over the weekend and falsely blamed the news media for making it up.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The notion of the United States doing the bidding of the Saudis has a long, bristling history. Critics complained that Saudi Arabia effectively hired out the American military to protect itself from Saddam Hussein’s Iraq and reverse his invasion of Kuwait in 1990.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The Saudi government even forked over $16 billion to reimburse the United States for about a quarter of the cost of the war that followed in 1991 — along with Kuwait, the most of any country.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The resentment felt over the years by American officials crossed the ideological spectrum, summed up pithily in a leaked 2010 cable by Defense Secretary Robert M. Gates, who served under Presidents George W. Bush and Barack Obama.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The Saudis, Mr. Gates told the French foreign minister at the time, always want to “fight the Iranians to the last American.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Among those who seemed to share the sentiment in the past was a New York businessman and television entertainer named Donald J. Trump.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“Saudi Arabia should fight their own wars, which they won’t, or pay us an absolute fortune to protect them and their great wealth-$ trillion!” <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://twitter.com/realdonaldtrump/status/506198852933013504?lang=en" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">he tweeted in 2014</a>.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Since taking office, Mr. Trump has made Saudi Arabia his closest ally in the Middle East other than Israel, and has strongly supported its multifront struggle with Iran for dominance in the region. He has also left little doubt about the primacy of money in the relationship, openly citing the value of arms contracts in explaining why he would not criticize the Saudi government for Mr. Khashoggi’s killing.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">When <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/14/world/middleeast/saudi-arabia-refineries-drone-attack.html?module=inline" title="">two Saudi oil processing centers were hit</a> by an aerial assault over the weekend, Mr. Trump spoke out quickly, much as any president might given the effect on world oil supplies.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“Saudi Arabia oil supply was attacked,” <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://twitter.com/realdonaldtrump/status/1173368423381962752" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">Mr. Trump tweeted</a>. “There is reason to believe that we know the culprit, are locked and loaded depending on verification, but are waiting to hear from the Kingdom as to who they believe was the cause of this attack, and under what terms we would proceed!”</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-79elbk" data-testid="photoviewer-wrapper"><div class="css-z3e15g" data-testid="photoviewer-wrapper-hidden"></div><div class="css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15" data-testid="photoviewer-children"><figure aria-label="media" class="css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0" itemid="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/16/us/politics/16dc-prexy3/merlin_157174200_c8103a0a-fa73-4fba-aa40-e21cbc9ebf1e-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp" itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" role="group"><div class="css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Image</span><div class="css-zjzyr8"><div data-testid="lazyimage-container" style="height:243.6px"></div></div></div><figcaption class="css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0" itemprop="caption description"><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0">Mr. Trump meeting with Mohammad bin Salman, the Saudi crown prince, during the Group of 20 summit in June in Osaka, Japan.</span><span class="css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90" itemprop="copyrightHolder"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Credit</span><span>Erin Schaff/The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The statement was strange for many reasons. Mr. Pompeo had already named the Iranians as the culprits; Mr. Trump did not. But the seeming abdication of fact-finding and decision-making to the Saudis gave Democrats a moment to argue that the president was willing to let the Saudi monarchy make decisions for the United States.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“If the President wants to use military force, he needs Congress, not the Saudi royal family, to authorize it,” Representative David Cicilline of Rhode Island, the chairman of the Democratic Policy and Communications Committee, <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://twitter.com/davidcicilline/status/1173387134864101378" rel="noopener noreferrer" target="_blank" title="">wrote on Twitter</a>.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Heather Hurlburt, a national security official under President Bill Clinton who is now at New America, a Washington-based research organization, said it would be perfectly normal for a president to consult an ally before taking action in such a circumstance.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“It’s not remotely normal for a president to talk publicly about that, to use language that sounds as if we aren’t making our own decisions about whether to use force — or trusting our own intelligence,” she said. “And it’s completely unprecedented with a country that is not a treaty ally.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The White House declined to comment on Monday beyond Mr. Trump’s remarks, but some national security conservatives were willing to give the president the benefit of the doubt.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“Obviously, it’s difficult to know for sure what’s going through the president’s mind,” said John P. Hannah, a senior counselor at the Foundation for Defense of Democracies in Washington and a former national security adviser to Vice President Dick Cheney.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">But he said that his guess was that Mr. Trump “wants the country most affected and threatened by the attack to step up publicly, pin responsibility squarely on Iran and put some real skin into the game by formally requesting that the U.S. and international community come to the defense of Saudi Arabia and the global economy.”</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">That could help mobilize international opinion and perhaps forge a coalition against Iran, “rather than an excuse to do nothing,” Mr. Hannah added.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">In his comments to reporters on Monday, Mr. Trump seemed intent on avoiding the perception that he was taking direction from the Saudis. If there is any response to the strikes on the oil facilities, he said, then the Saudis would play a part themselves — if nothing else, by financing it.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Which, of course, made it sound as if the United States was willing to be, in effect, a mercenary force for the Saudis.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“The fact is the Saudis are going to have a lot of involvement in this if we decide to do something,” he said. “They’ll be very much involved. And that includes payment. And they understand that fully.”</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div></section><div class="bottom-of-article"><div class="css-1ubp8k9"></div><div class="css-1yif149"><p>Michael Crowley contributed reporting.</p> </div><div class="css-vdv0al">A version of this article appears in print on <!-- -->, Section <!-- -->A<!-- -->, Page <!-- -->10<!-- --> of the New York edition<!-- --> with fill-rule="evenodd"></path></svg></button></div></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="css-12qsqia" id="related-coverage"><header class="css-1k2cc88"><h3 class="css-pk3ldd">Related Coverage</h3></header><div class="css-6su6fj"><a class="css-9efuks" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/14/world/middleeast/saudi-arabia-refineries-drone-attack.html?action=click&amp;module=RelatedCoverage&amp;pgtype=Article&amp;region=Footer"><div class="css-cmgnk4"><div class="css-dg19va"><p class="css-zdpruj e6idgb70"></p><div class="css-ip4ck2"><div><h2 class="css-65zpa8 eoo0vm40">Two Major Saudi Oil Installations Hit by Drone Strike, and U.S. Blames Iran</h2></div><time class="css-sehbwy e16638kd0" datetime="2019-09-14T08:35:11-04:00">Sept. 14, 2019</time></div></div><div class="css-161i88g"><figure aria-label="media" class="" class="css-dg19va"><p class="css-zdpruj e6idgb70"></p><div class="css-ip4ck2"><div><h2 class="css-65zpa8 eoo0vm40">Saudi Oil Attack Photos Implicate Iran, U.S. Says; Trump Hints at Military Action</h2></div><time class="css-sehbwy e16638kd0" datetime="2019-09-15T05:53:51-04:00">Sept. 15, 2019</time></div></div><div class="css-161i88g"><figure aria-label="media" class="" itemid="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/15/world/15iran/15iran-thumbLarge.jpg" itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" role="group"><div><span class="css-1dv1kvn">Image</span><div class="css-zjzyr8"><div data-testid="lazyimage-container" style="height:386.6666666666667px"></div></div></div><figcaption class="css-17ai7jg emkp2hg0" itemprop="caption description"></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class="css-1i15vd3"></div></a><a class="css-ljapoq" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/16/world/middleeast/saudi-oil.html?action=click&amp;module=RelatedCoverage&amp;pgtype=Article&amp;region=Footer"><div class="css-cmgnk4"><div class="css-dg19va"><p class="css-zdpruj e6idgb70"></p><div class="css-ip4ck2"><div><h2 class="css-65zpa8 eoo0vm40">Trump Says Iran Appears Responsible for Saudi Attack but That He Wants to Avoid
